\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1GhVBYNZAsGZtOfgo8C3VY/42fc180d060574162071cbdd13ad6a88/image6-6.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;Log        &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, we are excited to announce beta availability of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;Log Explorer&lt;/a&gt;, which allows you to investigate your HTTP and Security Event logs directly from the Cloudflare Dashboard. Log Explorer is an extension of &lt;a href=\&quot;/security-analytics\&quot;&gt;Security Analytics&lt;/a&gt;, giving you the ability to review related raw logs. You can analyze, investigate, and monitor for security attacks natively within the Cloudflare Dashboard, reducing time to resolution and overall cost of ownership by eliminating the need to forward logs to third party security analysis tools.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;background\&quot;&gt;Background&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#background\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Security Analytics enables you to analyze all of your HTTP traffic in one place, giving you the security lens you need to identify and act upon what matters most: potentially malicious traffic that has not been mitigated. Security Analytics includes built-in views such as top statistics and in-context quick filters on an intuitive page layout that enables rapid exploration and validation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In order to power our rich analytics dashboards with fast query performance, we implemented &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/analytics/graphql-api/sampling/\&quot;&gt;data sampling&lt;/a&gt; using &lt;a href=\&quot;/explaining-cloudflares-abr-analytics\&quot;&gt;Adaptive Bit Rate&lt;/a&gt; (ABR) analytics. This is a great fit for providing high level aggregate views of the data. However, we received feedback from many Security Analytics power users that sometimes they need access to a more granular view of the data â they need logs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Logs provide critical visibility into the operations of today&amp;#39;s computer systems. Engineers and SOC analysts rely on logs every day to troubleshoot issues, identify and investigate security incidents, and tune the performance, reliability, and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/solutions/\&quot;&gt;security&lt;/a&gt; of their applications and infrastructure. Traditional metrics or monitoring solutions provide aggregated or statistical data that can be used to identify trends. Metrics are wonderful at identifying THAT an issue happened, but lack the detailed events to help engineers uncover WHY it happened. Engineers and SOC Analysts rely on raw log data to answer questions such as:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;What is causing this increase in 403 errors?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;What data was accessed by this IP address?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;What was the user experience of this particular userâs session?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Traditionally, these engineers and analysts would stand up a collection of various monitoring tools in order to capture logs and get this visibility. With more organizations using multiple clouds, or a hybrid environment with both cloud and on-premise tools and architecture, it is crucial to have a unified platform to regain visibility into this increasingly complex environment. Â As more and more companies are moving towards a cloud native architecture, we see Cloudflareâs &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/en-gb/learning/cloud/what-is-a-connectivity-cloud/\&quot;&gt;connectivity cloud&lt;/a&gt; as an integral part of their performance and security strategy.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Log Explorer provides a lower cost option for storing and exploring log data within Cloudflare. Until today, we have offered the ability to export logs to expensive third party tools, and now with Log Explorer, you can quickly and easily explore your log data without leaving the Cloudflare Dashboard.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;log-explorer-features\&quot;&gt;Log Explorer Features&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#log-explorer-features\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Whether you&amp;#39;re a SOC Engineer investigating potential incidents, or a Compliance Officer with specific log retention requirements, Log Explorer has you covered. It stores your Cloudflare logs for an uncapped and customizable period of time, making them accessible natively within the Cloudflare Dashboard. The supported features include:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Searching through your HTTP Request or Security Event logs&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Filtering based on any field and a number of standard operators&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Switching between basic filter mode or SQL query interface&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Selecting fields to display&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Viewing log events in tabular format&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Finding the HTTP request records associated with a Ray ID&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;narrow-in-on-unmitigated-traffic\&quot;&gt;Narrow in on unmitigated traffic&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#narrow-in-on-unmitigated-traffic\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;As a SOC analyst, your job is to monitor and respond to threats and incidents within your organizationâs network. Using Security Analytics, and now with Log Explorer, you can identify anomalies and conduct a forensic investigation all in one place.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letâs walk through an example to see this in action:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;On the Security Analytics dashboard, you can see in the Insights panel that there is some traffic that has been tagged as a likely attack, but not mitigated.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5Oq3oqY8JXMigK8OJKPFZ4/5d3a8751a56f06f58e96538f1d46a480/Screenshot-2024-03-07-at-20.20.41.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;2000\&quot; height=\&quot;323\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Clicking the filter button narrows in on these requests for further investigation.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7sWkjUYz1J0So4nphy4FSs/769d5ebb0b706a073a616b706783030c/image11.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1844\&quot; height=\&quot;1018\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;In the sampled logs view, you can see that most of these requests are coming from a common client IP address.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5gtrP14GKbnB0YeV0ySgL1/6b476ec9d19e255912315eac9730604d/Sampled-logs.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;510\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can also see that Cloudflare has flagged all of these requests as bot traffic. With this information, you can craft a WAF rule to either block all traffic from this IP address, or block all traffic with a bot score lower than 10.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2YgFTRD7u3KYh0bbInLylK/f076a70bc09f41d8ace0569bca172b39/Screenshot-2024-03-07-at-20.22.04.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;2000\&quot; height=\&quot;407\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letâs say that the Compliance Team would like to gather documentation on the scope and impact of this attack. We can dig further into the logs during this time period to see everything that this attacker attempted to access.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;First, we can use Log Explorer to query HTTP requests from the suspect IP address during the time range of the spike seen in Security Analytics.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/qsi7UnxjtygCQHnMCIx02/cda0aacf6d783b05c15196f27907c611/Log-Explorer.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;510\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/YyewPADkPzjofXHXSihyi/e494ca5d4b9a3ad7071d5d3e27f57887/Query-results.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;852\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;We can also review whether the attacker was able to &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/what-is-data-exfiltration/\&quot;&gt;exfiltrate&lt;/a&gt; data by adding the OriginResponseBytes field and updating the query to show requests with OriginResponseBytes &amp;gt; 0. The results show that no data was exfiltrated.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3TgN2aPwWTDo5niA95TGQx/71143be92550dfea1ce284507fa688ac/No-logs-found.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;698\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;find-and-investigate-false-positives\&quot;&gt;Find and investigate false positives&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#find-and-investigate-false-positives\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;With access to the full logs via Log Explorer, you can now perform a search to find specific requests.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A 403 error occurs when a userâs request to a particular site is blocked. Cloudflareâs security products use things like &lt;a href=\&quot;/introducing-ip-lists/\&quot;&gt;IP reputation&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;/stop-attacks-before-they-are-known-making-the-cloudflare-waf-smarter/\&quot;&gt;WAF attack scores&lt;/a&gt; based on ML technologies in order to assess whether a given HTTP request is malicious. This is extremely effective, but sometimes requests are mistakenly flagged as malicious and blocked.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In these situations, we can now use Log Explorer to identify these requests and why they were blocked, and then adjust the relevant WAF rules accordingly.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5ecKfF4lRDQSyLCoOgDjTw/6f0872962caff8d719958e6fdfcc8dbc/Log-Explorer-2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;859\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Or, if you are interested in tracking down a specific request by Ray ID, an identifier given to every request that goes through Cloudflare, you can do that via Log Explorer with one query.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3NCDOP0axFC3wZ4qs03Jei/86286da2fd9fca3cdb68214c1d0f472a/Log-Explorer-3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;750\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Note that the LIMIT clause is included in the query by default, but has no impact on RayID queries as RayID is unique and only one record would be returned when using the RayID filter field.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-we-built-log-explorer\&quot;&gt;How we built Log Explorer&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-we-built-log-explorer\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        \n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3pNBd5iSyVW7aqfJ0JfYDP/89cd0341cc35ad9d86fd8687ba7a9147/How-we-built-Log-Explorer.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;1191\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;With Log Explorer, we have built a long-term, append-only log storage platform on top of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/developer-platform/r2/\&quot;&gt;Cloudflare R2&lt;/a&gt;. Log Explorer leverages the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://databricks.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/p975-armbrust.pdf\&quot;&gt;Delta Lake&lt;/a&gt; protocol, an open-source storage framework for building highly performant, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ACID\&quot;&gt;ACID&lt;/a&gt;-compliant databases atop a cloud object store. In other words, Log Explorer combines a large and cost-effective storage system â &lt;a href=\&quot;www.cloudflare.com/developer-platform/r2/\&quot;&gt;Cloudflare R2&lt;/a&gt; â with the benefits of strong consistency and high performance. Additionally, Log Explorer gives you a SQL interface to your Cloudflare logs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Each Log Explorer dataset is stored on a per-customer level, just like Cloudflare D1, so that your data isn&amp;#39;t placed with that of other customers. In the future, this single-tenant storage model will give you the flexibility to create your own retention policies and decide in which regions you want to store your data.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Under the hood, the datasets for each customer are stored as Delta tables in R2 buckets. A &lt;i&gt;Delta table&lt;/i&gt; is a storage format that organizes Apache Parquet objects into directories using Hive&amp;#39;s partitioning naming convention. Crucially, Delta tables pair these storage objects with an append-only, checkpointed transaction log. This design allows Log Explorer to support multiple writers with optimistic concurrency.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Many of the products Cloudflare builds are a direct result of the challenges our own team is looking to address. Log Explorer is a perfect example of this &lt;a href=\&quot;/tag/dogfooding\&quot;&gt;culture of dogfooding&lt;/a&gt;. Optimistic concurrent writes require atomic updates in the underlying object store, and as a result of our needs, R2 added a PutIfAbsent operation with strong consistency. Thanks, R2! The atomic operation sets Log Explorer apart from Delta Lake solutions based on Amazon Web Servicesâ S3, which incur the operational burden of using an &lt;a href=\&quot;https://delta.io/blog/2022-05-18-multi-cluster-writes-to-delta-lake-storage-in-s3/\&quot;&gt;external store&lt;/a&gt; for synchronizing writes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Log Explorer is written in the Rust programming language using open-source libraries, such as &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/delta-io/delta-rs\&quot;&gt;delta-rs&lt;/a&gt;, a native Rust implementation of the Delta Lake protocol, and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://arrow.apache.org/datafusion/\&quot;&gt;Apache Arrow DataFusion&lt;/a&gt;, a very fast, extensible query engine. At Cloudflare, Rust has emerged as a popular choice for new product development due to its safety and performance benefits.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;whats-next\&quot;&gt;Whatâs next&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#whats-next\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;We know that application security logs are only part of the puzzle in understanding whatâs going on in your environment. Stay tuned for future developments including tighter, more seamless integration between Analytics and Log Explorer, the addition of more datasets including Zero Trust logs, the ability to define custom retention periods, and integrated custom alerting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Please use the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://forms.gle/tvKQDdXmCk98zyV9A\&quot;&gt;feedback link&lt;/a&gt; to let us know how Log Explorer is working for you and what else would help make your job easier.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-to-get-it\&quot;&gt;How to get it&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-to-get-it\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Weâd love to hear from you! Let us know if you are interested in joining our Beta program by completing &lt;a href=\&quot;https://cloudflare.com/lp/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;this form&lt;/a&gt; and a member of our team will contact you.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Pricing will be finalized prior to a General Availability (GA) launch.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;!--kg-card-begin: html--&gt;&lt;div style=\&quot;position: relative; padding-top: 56.25%;\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;iframe\n    src=\&quot;https://customer-rhnwzxvb3mg4wz3v.cloudflarestream.com/3634e036c083187e181b7b88db1e2777/iframe?preload=true&amp;poster=https%3A%2F%2Fcustomer-rhnwzxvb3mg4wz3v.cloudflarestream.com%2F3634e036c083187e181b7b88db1e2777%2Fthumbnails%2Fthumbnail.jpg%3Ftime%3D%26height%3D600\&quot;\n    loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;\n    style=\&quot;border: none; position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; height: 100%; width: 100%;\&quot;\n    allow=\&quot;accelerometer; gyroscope; autoplay; encrypted-media; picture-in-picture;\&quot;\n    allowfullscreen=\&quot;true\&quot;\n  &gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;&lt;!--kg-card-end: html--&gt;&lt;p&gt;Tune in for more news, announcements and thought-provoking discussions! SIEMs&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card \&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image third-party storage\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1125\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, we are excited to announce beta availability of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/log-explorer/\&quot;&gt;Log Explorer&lt;/a&gt;, which allows you to investigate your HTTP and Security Event logs directly from the Cloudflare Dashboard. Log Explorer is an extension of &lt;a href=\&quot;/security-analytics\&quot;&gt;Security Analytics&lt;/a&gt;, giving you the ability to review related raw logs. You can analyze, investigate, and monitor for security attacks natively within the Cloudflare Dashboard, reducing time to resolution and overall cost of ownership by eliminating the need to forward logs to third party security analysis tools.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;background\&quot;&gt;Background&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#background\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Security Analytics enables you to analyze all of your HTTP traffic in one place, giving you the security lens you need to identify and act upon what matters most: potentially malicious traffic that has not been mitigated. Security Analytics includes built-in views such as top statistics and in-context quick filters on an intuitive page layout that enables rapid exploration and validation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In order to power our rich analytics dashboards with fast query performance, we implemented &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/analytics/graphql-api/sampling/\&quot;&gt;data sampling&lt;/a&gt; using &lt;a href=\&quot;/explaining-cloudflares-abr-analytics\&quot;&gt;Adaptive Bit Rate&lt;/a&gt; (ABR) analytics. This is a great fit for providing high level aggregate views of the data. However, we received feedback from many Security Analytics power users that sometimes they need access to a more granular view of the data â they need logs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Logs provide critical visibility into the operations of today&amp;#39;s computer systems. Engineers and SOC analysts rely on logs every day to troubleshoot issues, identify and investigate security incidents, and tune the performance, reliability, and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/application-services/solutions/\&quot;&gt;security&lt;/a&gt; of their applications and infrastructure. Traditional metrics or monitoring solutions provide aggregated or statistical data that can be used to identify trends. Metrics are wonderful at identifying THAT an issue happened, but lack the detailed events to help engineers uncover WHY it happened. Engineers and SOC Analysts rely on raw log data to answer questions such as:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;What is causing this increase in 403 errors?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;What data was accessed by this IP address?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;What was the user experience of this particular userâs session?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Traditionally, these engineers and analysts would stand up a collection of various monitoring tools in order to capture logs and get this visibility. With more organizations using multiple clouds, or a hybrid environment with both cloud and on-premise tools and architecture, it is crucial to have a unified platform to regain visibility into this increasingly complex environment. Â As more and more companies are moving towards a cloud native architecture, we see Cloudflareâs &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/en-gb/learning/cloud/what-is-a-connectivity-cloud/\&quot;&gt;connectivity cloud&lt;/a&gt; as an integral part of their performance and security strategy.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Log Explorer provides a lower cost option for storing and exploring log data within Cloudflare. Until today, we have offered the ability to export logs to expensive third party tools, and now with Log Explorer, you can quickly and easily explore your log data without leaving the Cloudflare Dashboard.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;log-explorer-features\&quot;&gt;Log Explorer Features&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#log-explorer-features\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Whether you&amp;#39;re a SOC Engineer investigating potential incidents, or a Compliance Officer with specific log retention requirements, Log Explorer has you covered. It stores your Cloudflare logs for an uncapped and customizable period of time, making them accessible natively within the Cloudflare Dashboard. The supported features include:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Searching through your HTTP Request or Security Event logs&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Filtering based on any field and a number of standard operators&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Switching between basic filter mode or SQL query interface&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Selecting fields to display&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Viewing log events in tabular format&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Finding the HTTP request records associated with a Ray ID&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;narrow-in-on-unmitigated-traffic\&quot;&gt;Narrow in on unmitigated traffic&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#narrow-in-on-unmitigated-traffic\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;As a SOC analyst, your job is to monitor and respond to threats and incidents within your organizationâs network. Using Security Analytics, and now with Log Explorer, you can identify anomalies and conduct a forensic investigation all in one place.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letâs walk through an example to see this in action:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;On the Security Analytics dashboard, you can see in the Insights panel that there is some traffic that has been tagged as a likely attack, but not mitigated.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5Oq3oqY8JXMigK8OJKPFZ4/5d3a8751a56f06f58e96538f1d46a480/Screenshot-2024-03-07-at-20.20.41.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;2000\&quot; height=\&quot;323\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Clicking the filter button narrows in on these requests for further investigation.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7sWkjUYz1J0So4nphy4FSs/769d5ebb0b706a073a616b706783030c/image11.jpg\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1844\&quot; height=\&quot;1018\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;In the sampled logs view, you can see that most of these requests are coming from a common client IP address.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5gtrP14GKbnB0YeV0ySgL1/6b476ec9d19e255912315eac9730604d/Sampled-logs.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;510\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can also see that Cloudflare has flagged all of these requests as bot traffic. With this information, you can craft a WAF rule to either block all traffic from this IP address, or block all traffic with a bot score lower than 10.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2YgFTRD7u3KYh0bbInLylK/f076a70bc09f41d8ace0569bca172b39/Screenshot-2024-03-07-at-20.22.04.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;2000\&quot; height=\&quot;407\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letâs say that the Compliance Team would like to gather documentation on the scope and impact of this attack. We can dig further into the logs during this time period to see everything that this attacker attempted to access.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;First, we can use Log Explorer to query HTTP requests from the suspect IP address during the time range of the spike seen in Security Analytics.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/qsi7UnxjtygCQHnMCIx02/cda0aacf6d783b05c15196f27907c611/Log-Explorer.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;510\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/YyewPADkPzjofXHXSihyi/e494ca5d4b9a3ad7071d5d3e27f57887/Query-results.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;852\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;We can also review whether the attacker was able to &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/what-is-data-exfiltration/\&quot;&gt;exfiltrate&lt;/a&gt; data by adding the OriginResponseBytes field and updating the query to show requests with OriginResponseBytes &amp;gt; 0. The results show that no data was exfiltrated.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3TgN2aPwWTDo5niA95TGQx/71143be92550dfea1ce284507fa688ac/No-logs-found.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;698\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;find-and-investigate-false-positives\&quot;&gt;Find and investigate false positives&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#find-and-investigate-false-positives\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;With access to the full logs via Log Explorer, you can now perform a search to find specific requests.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A 403 error occurs when a userâs request to a particular site is blocked. Cloudflareâs security products use things like &lt;a href=\&quot;/introducing-ip-lists/\&quot;&gt;IP reputation&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;/stop-attacks-before-they-are-known-making-the-cloudflare-waf-smarter/\&quot;&gt;WAF attack scores&lt;/a&gt; based on ML technologies in order to assess whether a given HTTP request is malicious. This is extremely effective, but sometimes requests are mistakenly flagged as malicious and blocked.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In these situations, we can now use Log Explorer to identify these requests and why they were blocked, and then adjust the relevant WAF rules accordingly.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5ecKfF4lRDQSyLCoOgDjTw/6f0872962caff8d719958e6fdfcc8dbc/Log-Explorer-2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;859\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Or, if you are interested in tracking down a specific request by Ray ID, an identifier given to every request that goes through Cloudflare, you can do that via Log Explorer with one query.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3NCDOP0axFC3wZ4qs03Jei/86286da2fd9fca3cdb68214c1d0f472a/Log-Explorer-3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;750\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Note that the LIMIT clause is included in the query by default, but has no impact on RayID queries as RayID is unique and only one record would be returned when using the RayID filter field.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-we-built-log-explorer\&quot;&gt;How we built Log Explorer&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-we-built-log-explorer\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        \n            &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card kg-width-wide\&quot;&gt;\n            \n            &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3pNBd5iSyVW7aqfJ0JfYDP/89cd0341cc35ad9d86fd8687ba7a9147/How-we-built-Log-Explorer.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;1191\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n            \n            &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;With Log Explorer, we have built a long-term, append-only log storage platform on top of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/developer-platform/r2/\&quot;&gt;Cloudflare R2&lt;/a&gt;. Log Explorer leverages the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://databricks.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/p975-armbrust.pdf\&quot;&gt;Delta Lake&lt;/a&gt; protocol, an open-source storage framework for building highly performant, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ACID\&quot;&gt;ACID&lt;/a&gt;-compliant databases atop a cloud object store. In other words, Log Explorer combines a large and cost-effective storage system â &lt;a href=\&quot;www.cloudflare.com/developer-platform/r2/\&quot;&gt;Cloudflare R2&lt;/a&gt; â with the benefits of strong consistency and high performance. Additionally, Log Explorer gives you a SQL interface to your Cloudflare logs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Each Log Explorer dataset is stored on a per-customer level, just like Cloudflare D1, so that your data isn&amp;#39;t placed with that of other customers. In the future, this single-tenant storage model will give you the flexibility to create your own retention policies and decide in which regions you want to store your data.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Under the hood, the datasets for each customer are stored as Delta tables in R2 buckets. A &lt;i&gt;Delta table&lt;/i&gt; is a storage format that organizes Apache Parquet objects into directories using Hive&amp;#39;s partitioning naming convention. Crucially, Delta tables pair these storage objects with an append-only, checkpointed transaction log. This design allows Log Explorer to support multiple writers with optimistic concurrency.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Many of the products Cloudflare builds are a direct result of the challenges our own team is looking to address. Log Explorer is a perfect example of this &lt;a href=\&quot;/tag/dogfooding\&quot;&gt;culture of dogfooding&lt;/a&gt;. Optimistic concurrent writes require atomic updates in the underlying object store, and as a result of our needs, R2 added a PutIfAbsent operation with strong consistency. Thanks, R2! The atomic operation sets Log Explorer apart from Delta Lake solutions based on Amazon Web Servicesâ S3, which incur the operational burden of using an &lt;a href=\&quot;https://delta.io/blog/2022-05-18-multi-cluster-writes-to-delta-lake-storage-in-s3/\&quot;&gt;external store&lt;/a&gt; for synchronizing writes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Log Explorer is written in the Rust programming language using open-source libraries, such as &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/delta-io/delta-rs\&quot;&gt;delta-rs&lt;/a&gt;, a native Rust implementation of the Delta Lake protocol, and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://arrow.apache.org/datafusion/\&quot;&gt;Apache Arrow DataFusion&lt;/a&gt;, a very fast, extensible query engine. At Cloudflare, Rust has emerged as a popular choice for new product development due to its safety and performance benefits.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;whats-next\&quot;&gt;Whatâs next&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#whats-next\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;We know that application security logs are only part of the puzzle in understanding whatâs going on in your environment. Stay tuned for future developments including tighter, more seamless integration between Analytics and Log Explorer, the addition of more datasets including Zero Trust logs, the ability to define custom retention periods, and integrated custom alerting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Please use the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://forms.gle/tvKQDdXmCk98zyV9A\&quot;&gt;feedback link&lt;/a&gt; to let us know how Log Explorer is working for you and what else would help make your job easier.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-to-get-it\&quot;&gt;How to get it&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-to-get-it\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Weâd love to hear from you! incident on November 14, 2024, resulting in lost logs&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;cloudflare-incident-on-november-14-2024-resulting-in-lost-logs&quot;],&quot;excerpt&quot;:[0,&quot;On November 14, 2024, Cloudflare experienced a Cloudflare Logs outage, impacting the majority of customers using these products. During the ~3.5 hours that these services were impacted, about 55% of the logs we normally send to customers were not sent and were lost. The details of what went wrong and why are interesting both for customers and practitioners.&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;On November 14, 2024, Cloudflare experienced an incident which impacted the majority of customers using &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Logs&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. During the roughly 3.5 hours that these services were impacted, about 55% of the logs we normally send to customers were not sent and were lost. Weâre very sorry this happened, and we are working to ensure that a similar issue doesn&amp;#39;t happen again.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This blog post explains what happened and what weâre doing to prevent recurrences. Also, the systems involved and the particular class of failure we experienced will hopefully be of interest to engineering teams beyond those specifically using these products.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Failures within systems at scale are inevitable, and itâs essential that subsystems protect themselves from failures in other parts of the larger system to prevent cascades. In this case, a misconfiguration in one part of the system caused a cascading overload in another part of the system, which was itself misconfigured. Had it been properly configured, it could have prevented the loss of logs.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;background\&quot;&gt;Background&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#background\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;Cloudflareâs network is a globally distributed system enabling and supporting a wide variety of services. Every part of this system generates event logs which contain detailed metadata about whatâs happening with our systems around the world. For example, an event log is generated for every request to Cloudflareâs CDN. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.c/om/logs\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Logs&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; makes these event logs available to customers, who use them in a number of ways, including compliance, observability, and accounting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;On a typical day, Cloudflare sends about 4.5 trillion individual event logs to customers. Although this represents less than 10% of the over 50 trillion total customer event logs processed, it presents unique challenges of scale when building a reliable and fault-tolerant system.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;system-architecture\&quot;&gt;System architecture&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#system-architecture\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;Cloudflareâs network is composed of tens of thousands of individual servers, network hardware components, and specialized software programs located in over 330 cities around the world. Although Cloudflareâs &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/edge-log-delivery/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Edge Log Delivery&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; product will send customers their event logs directly from each server, most customers opt not to do this because doing so will create significant complication and cost at the receiving end.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;By analogy, imagine the postal service ringing your doorbell once for each letter instead of once for each packet of letters. With thousands or millions of letters each second, the number of separate transactions that would entail becomes prohibitive.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Fortunately, we also offer &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/about/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Logpush&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which collects and pushes logs to customers in more predictable file sizes and which scales automatically with usage. In order to provide this feature several services work together to collect and push the logs, as illustrated in the diagram below:&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6pRdzUUrMbwG3AWsPncB3w/75146d1e379ccb126d8cd0210a6c12b8/image2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1480\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;logfwdr\&quot;&gt;Logfwdr&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#logfwdr\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Logfwdr is an internal service written in Golang that accepts event logs from internal services running across Cloudflareâs global network and forwards them in batches to a service called Logreceiver. Logfwdr handles many different types of event logs, and one of its responsibilities is to determine which event logs should be forwarded and where they should be sent based on the type of event log, which customers it represents, and associated rules about where it should be processed. Configuration is provided to Logfwdr to enable it to make these determinations.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;logreceiver\&quot;&gt;Logreceiver&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#logreceiver\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Logreceiver (also written in Golang) accepts the batches of logs from across Cloudflareâs global network and further sorts them depending on the type of event and its purpose. For Cloudflare Logs, Logreceiver demultiplexes the batches into per-customer batches and forwards them to be buffered by Buftee. Currently, Logreceiver is handling about 45 PB (uncompressed) of customer event logs each day.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;buftee\&quot;&gt;Buftee&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#buftee\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Itâs common for data pipelines to include a buffer. Producers and consumers of the data might be operating at different cadences, and parts of the pipeline will experience variances in how quickly they can process information. Using a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_buffer\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;buffer&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; makes it easier to manage these situations, and helps to prevent data loss if downstream consumers are broken. Itâs also convenient to have a buffer that supports multiple downstream consumers with different cadences (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tee_(command)\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;like the pipe fitting function of a tee&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;At Cloudflare, we use an internal system called Buftee (written in Golang) to support this combined function. Buftee is a highly distributed system which supports a large number of named âbuffersâ. It supports operating on named âprefixesâ (collections of buffers) as well as multiple representations/resolutions of the same time-indexed dataset. Using Buftee makes it possible for Cloudflare to handle extremely high throughput very efficiently.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For Cloudflare Logs, Buftee provides buffers for each Logpush job, containing 100% of the logs generated by the zone or account referenced by each job. This means that failure to process one customerâs job will not affect progress on another customerâs job. Handling buffers in this way avoids âhead of lineâ blocking and also enables us to encrypt and delete each customerâs data separately if needed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Buftee typically handles over 1 million buffers globally. The following is a snapshot of the number of buffers managed by Buftee servers in the period just prior to the incident.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5g4Ev1CX8pGqtpNUY3vZOo/50d8dfa7a1e9c492a537e4822d801625/image5.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;735\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;logpush\&quot;&gt;Logpush&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#logpush\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Logpush is a Golang service which reads logs from Buftee buffers and pushes the results in batches to various destinations configured by customers. A batch could end up, for example, as a file in R2. Each job has a unique configuration, and only jobs that are active and configured will be pushed. Currently, we push over 600 million such batches each day.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;what-happened\&quot;&gt;What happened&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-happened\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;On November 14, 2024, we made a change to support an additional &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/reference/log-fields/#datasets\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;dataset&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for Logpush. This required adding a new configuration to be provided to Logfwdr in order for it to know which customersâ logs to forward for this new stream. Every few minutes, a separate system re-generates the configuration used by Logfwdr to decide which logs need to be forwarded. A bug in this system resulted in a blank configuration being provided to Logfwdr.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This bug essentially informed Logfwdr that &lt;b&gt;no customers&lt;/b&gt; had logs configured to be pushed. The team quickly noticed the mistake and reverted the change in under five minutes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Unfortunately, this first mistake triggered a second, latent bug in Logfwdr itself. A failsafe introduced in the early days of this feature, when traffic was much lower, was configured to âfail openâ. This failsafe was designed to protect against a situation when this specific Logfwdr configuration was unavailable (as in this case) by transmitting events for &lt;b&gt;all customers&lt;/b&gt; instead of just those who had configured a Logpush job. This was intended to prevent the loss of logs at the expense of sending more logs than strictly necessary when individual hosts were prevented from getting the configuration due to intermittent networking errors, for example.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When this failsafe was first introduced, the potential list of customers was smaller than it is today. This small window of less than five minutes resulted in a massive spike&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;in the number of customers whose logs were sent by Logfwdr.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Even given this massive overload, our systems would have continued to send logs if not for one additional problem. Remember that Buftee creates a separate buffer for each customer with their logs to be pushed. When Logfwdr began to send event logs for all customers, Buftee began to create buffers for each one as those logs arrived, and each buffer requires resources as well as the bookkeeping to maintain them. This massive increase, resulting in roughly 40 times more buffers, is not something weâve provisioned Buftee clusters to handle. In the lead-up to impact, Buftee was managing 40 million buffers globally, as shown in the figure below.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7HPwhkvRxiAQtjVbdVxRUN/a1d4aa174961f6a163e884011c8c18ad/image3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;735\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;A short temporary misconfiguration lasting just five minutes created a massive overload that took us several hours to fix and recover from. Because our backstops were not properly configured, the underlying systems became so overloaded that we could not interact with them normally.Â  A full reset and restart was required.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;root-causes\&quot;&gt;Root causes&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#root-causes\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;The bug in the Logfwdr configuration system was easy to fix, but itâs the type of bug that was likely to happen at some point.Â  We had planned for it by designing the original âfail openâ behavior.Â  However, we neglected to regularly test that the broader system was capable of handling a fail open event.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The bigger failure was that Buftee became unresponsive.Â  Bufteeâs purpose is to be a safeguard against bugs like this one.Â  A huge increase in the number of buffers is a failure mode that we had predicted, and had put mechanisms in Buftee to prevent this failure from cascading.Â  Our failure in this case was that we had not configured these mechanisms.Â  Had they been configured correctly, Buftee would not have been overwhelmed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;It&amp;#39;s like having a seatbelt in a car, yet not fastening it. The seatbelt is there to protect you in case of an accident but if you don&amp;#39;t actually buckle it up, it&amp;#39;s not going to do its job when you need it. Similarly, while we had the safeguard of Buftee in place, we hadn&amp;#39;t &amp;#39;buckled it up&amp;#39; by configuring the necessary settings. Weâre very sorry this happened and are taking steps to prevent a recurrence as described below.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;going-forward\&quot;&gt;Going forward&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#going-forward\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;Weâre creating alerts to ensure that these particular misconfigurations will be impossible to miss, and we are also addressing the specific bug and the associated tests that triggered this incident.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Just as importantly, we accept that mistakes and misconfigurations are inevitable. All our systems at Cloudflare need to respond to these predictably and gracefully. Currently, we conduct regular âcut testsâ to ensure that these systems will cope with the loss of a datacenter or a network failure. In the future, weâll also conduct regular âoverload testsâ to simulate the kind of cascade which happened in this incident to ensure that our production systems will handle them gracefully.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Logpush is a robust and flexible platform for customers who need to integrate their own logging and monitoring systems with Cloudflare. Different Logpush jobs can be deployed to support multiple destinations or, with filtering, multiple subsets of logs.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;],&quot;published_at&quot;:[0,&quot;2024-11-26T16:00+00:00&quot;],&quot;updated_at&quot;:[0,&quot;2024-11-26T16:11:03.020Z&quot;],&quot;feature_image&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/39YRp8HFKgOXjsatyJe1Z3/4f96f5d726460c0659d3cd7b63927347/image1.png&quot;],&quot;tags&quot;:[1,[[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;4fkY3bvsgn5JfTgXxTZHIR&quot;],&quot;name&quot;:[0,&quot;Logs&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;logs&quot;]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;5fXI7jwkVL8rNyKrfpk0Lw&quot;],&quot;name&quot;:[0,&quot;Data&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;data&quot;]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;51FqLJDNXq37C9HCXLSRH9&quot;],&quot;name&quot;:[0,&quot;Log
